<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Scottish Parliament</h1>			<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">

				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the present-day legislature. For the building housing it, see <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament_Building" title="Scottish Parliament Building">Scottish Parliament Building</a>. For the national legislature before 1707, see <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Scotland" title="Parliament of Scotland">Parliament of Scotland</a>.</div>

<p><br />
</p>
</div></div></div></td>
</tr><tr><td style="padding:0.3em 0.4em 0.3em;font-weight:bold;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; border-bottom: 1px solid #aaa;">
<a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Scotland.svg" class="image"><img alt="Flag of Scotland.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Flag_of_Scotland.svg/32px-Flag_of_Scotland.svg.png" width="32" height="19" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Flag_of_Scotland.svg/48px-Flag_of_Scotland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Flag_of_Scotland.svg/64px-Flag_of_Scotland.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Scotland" title="Portal:Scotland">Scotland&#32;portal</a>  <div class="hlist" style="text-align:center;font-weight:normal;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Outline_of_political_science#Politics_by_region" title="Outline of political science">Other countries</a></li>
<li><a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Atlas_of_Scotland" class="extiw" title="commons:Atlas of Scotland">Atlas</a></li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Politics_of_Scotland" title="Template:Politics of Scotland"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Politics_of_Scotland" title="Template talk:Politics of Scotland"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Politics_of_Scotland&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>Scottish Parliament</b> (<a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Gaelic language">Scottish Gaelic</a>: <i lang="gd">Pàrlamaid na h-Alba</i>; <a href="/wiki/Scots_language" title="Scots language">Scots</a>: <i>The Scots Pairlament</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> is the <a href="/wiki/Devolution" title="Devolution">devolved</a> national, <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> legislature of <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>. Located in the <a href="/wiki/Holyrood,_Edinburgh" title="Holyrood, Edinburgh">Holyrood</a> area of the capital city, <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>, it is frequently referred to by the <a href="/wiki/Metonymy" title="Metonymy">metonym</a> <b>Holyrood</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Parliament is a democratically elected body comprising 129 members known as <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_Scottish_Parliament" title="Member of the Scottish Parliament">Members of the Scottish Parliament</a> (MSPs), elected for four-year terms under the <a href="/wiki/Additional_member_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Additional member system">additional member system</a>: 73 MSPs represent individual geographical <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament_constituencies_and_regions" title="Scottish Parliament constituencies and regions">constituencies</a> elected by the <a href="/wiki/Plurality_voting_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Plurality voting system">plurality</a> ("first past the post") system, while a further 56 are returned from eight <a href="/wiki/Additional_Member_System" title="Additional Member System">additional member</a> regions, each electing seven MSPs.<sup id="cite_ref-ScotParlWorks_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ScotParlWorks-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The most recent <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament_election,_2016" title="Scottish Parliament election, 2016">general election</a> to the Parliament was held on 5 May 2016, with the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">Scottish National Party</a> winning a plurality.
</p><p>The original <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Scotland" title="Parliament of Scotland">Parliament of Scotland</a> was the national legislature of the independent <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Scotland" title="Kingdom of Scotland">Kingdom of Scotland</a>, and existed from the early 13th century until the Kingdom of Scotland merged with the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">Kingdom of England</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union_1707" title="Acts of Union 1707">Acts of Union 1707</a> to form the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Kingdom of Great Britain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HistoricalConnection_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistoricalConnection-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> As a consequence, both the Parliament of Scotland and the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_England" title="Parliament of England">Parliament of England</a> ceased to exist, and the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Great_Britain" title="Parliament of Great Britain">Parliament of Great Britain</a>, which sat at <a href="/wiki/Westminster" title="Westminster">Westminster</a> in London<sup id="cite_ref-HistoricalConnection_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistoricalConnection-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> was formed.
</p><p>Following a <a href="/wiki/Scottish_devolution_referendum,_1997" title="Scottish devolution referendum, 1997">referendum in 1997</a>, in which the Scottish electorate voted for devolution, the powers of the <a href="/wiki/Devolution" title="Devolution">devolved</a> legislature were specified by the <a href="/wiki/Scotland_Act_1998" title="Scotland Act 1998">Scotland Act 1998</a>. The Act delineates the legislative competence of the Parliament – the areas in which it can make <a href="/wiki/Scots_law" title="Scots law">laws</a> – by explicitly specifying powers that are "<a href="/wiki/Reserved_matters" class="mw-redirect" title="Reserved matters">reserved</a>" to the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Parliament of the United Kingdom</a>. The Scottish Parliament has the power to legislate in all areas that are not explicitly reserved to Westminster.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The British Parliament retains the ability to amend the terms of reference of the Scottish Parliament, and can extend or reduce the areas in which it can make laws.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The first meeting of the new Parliament took place on 12 May 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The competence of the Scottish Parliament has been amended numerous times since then, most notably by the <a href="/wiki/Scotland_Act_2012" title="Scotland Act 2012">Scotland Act 2012</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scotland_Act_2016" title="Scotland Act 2016">Scotland Act 2016</a>, with some of the most significant changes being the expansion of the Parliament's powers over taxation and welfare.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History_of_the_Scottish_Parliament">History of the Scottish Parliament</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History of the Scottish Parliament">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Scottish_devolution" title="History of Scottish devolution">History of Scottish devolution</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Scottish_Parliament_logo.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/af/Scottish_Parliament_logo.png/220px-Scottish_Parliament_logo.png" width="220" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/af/Scottish_Parliament_logo.png/330px-Scottish_Parliament_logo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/a/af/Scottish_Parliament_logo.png 2x" data-file-width="349" data-file-height="286" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Scottish_Parliament_logo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Official logo of the Scottish Parliament</div></div></div>
<p>Before the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Union_1707" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Union 1707">Treaty of Union 1707</a> united the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Scotland" title="Kingdom of Scotland">Kingdom of Scotland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">Kingdom of England</a> into a new state called "<a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Great Britain</a>", Scotland had an <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">independent</a> parliament known as the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Scotland" title="Parliament of Scotland">Parliament of Scotland</a>. Initial Scottish proposals in the negotiation over the Union suggested a devolved Parliament be retained in Scotland, but this was not accepted by the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">English</a> negotiators.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>For the next three hundred years, Scotland was directly governed by the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Great_Britain" title="Parliament of Great Britain">Parliament of Great Britain</a> and the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Parliament of the United Kingdom</a>, both seated at Westminster, and the lack of a Parliament of Scotland remained an important element in <a href="/wiki/Scottish_national_identity" title="Scottish national identity">Scottish national identity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Devolution_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Devolution-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Suggestions for a 'devolved' Parliament were made before 1914, but were shelved due to the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">First World War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Devolution_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Devolution-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> A sharp rise in nationalism in Scotland during the late 1960s fuelled demands for some form of <a href="/wiki/Devolution" title="Devolution">home rule</a> or complete <a href="/wiki/Scottish_independence" title="Scottish independence">independence</a>, and in 1969 prompted the incumbent <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> government of <a href="/wiki/Harold_Wilson" title="Harold Wilson">Harold Wilson</a> to set up the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Commission_on_the_Constitution_(United_Kingdom)" title="Royal Commission on the Constitution (United Kingdom)">Kilbrandon Commission</a> to consider the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Constitution of the United Kingdom">British constitution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Devolution_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Devolution-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> One of the principal objectives of the commission was to examine ways of enabling more self-government for Scotland, within the unitary state of the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-Devolution_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Devolution-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Kilbrandon published his report in 1973 recommending the establishment of a directly elected <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Assembly" title="Scottish Assembly">Scottish Assembly</a> to legislate for the majority of domestic Scottish affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During this time, the discovery of <a href="/wiki/North_Sea_oil" title="North Sea oil">oil</a> in the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> and the following "<a href="/wiki/It%27s_Scotland%27s_oil" title="It&#39;s Scotland&#39;s oil">It's Scotland's oil</a>" campaign of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">Scottish National Party</a> (SNP) resulted in rising support for Scottish independence, as well as the SNP. The party argued that the revenues from the oil were not benefitting Scotland as much as they should.<sup id="cite_ref-Devolution_13-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Devolution-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The combined effect of these events led to <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister</a> Wilson committing his government to some form of devolved legislature in 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-Devolution_13-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Devolution-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> However, it was not until 1978 that final legislative proposals for a Scottish Assembly were passed by the United Kingdom Parliament.
</p><p>Under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Scotland_Act_1978" title="Scotland Act 1978">Scotland Act 1978</a>, an elected assembly would be set up in Edinburgh provided that a referendum be held on 1 March 1979, with at least 40% of the total electorate voting in favour of the proposal. The <a href="/wiki/Scottish_devolution_referendum,_1979" title="Scottish devolution referendum, 1979">1979 Scottish devolution referendum</a> failed:  although the vote was 51.6% in favour of a Scottish Assembly, with a turnout of 63.6%, the majority represented only 32.9% of the eligible voting population.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Throughout the 1980s and 1990s, demand for a Scottish Parliament grew, in part because the government of the United Kingdom was controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative Party</a>, while Scotland itself elected relatively few Conservative MPs.<sup id="cite_ref-Devolution_13-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Devolution-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> In the aftermath of the 1979 referendum defeat, the <a href="/wiki/Campaign_for_a_Scottish_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="Campaign for a Scottish Assembly">Campaign for a Scottish Assembly</a> was initiated as a <a href="/wiki/Pressure_group" class="mw-redirect" title="Pressure group">pressure group</a>, leading to the 1989 <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Constitutional_Convention" title="Scottish Constitutional Convention">Scottish Constitutional Convention</a> with various organisations such as <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Scotland" title="Religion in Scotland">Scottish churches</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Scotland" title="List of political parties in Scotland">political parties</a> and representatives of industry taking part. Publishing its blueprint for devolution in 1995, the Convention provided much of the basis for the structure of the Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<p>Devolution continued to be part of the platform of the Labour Party which, in May 1997, took power under <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Devolution_13-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Devolution-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> In September 1997, the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_devolution_referendum,_1997" title="Scottish devolution referendum, 1997">1997 Scottish devolution referendum</a> was put to the Scottish electorate and secured a majority in favour of the establishment of a new devolved Scottish Parliament, with tax-varying powers, in Edinburgh.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> An election was held on 6 May 1999, and on 1 July of that year power was transferred from Westminster to the new Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Building_and_grounds">Building and grounds</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Building and grounds">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament_Building" title="Scottish Parliament Building">Scottish Parliament Building</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ScottishParliamentFront.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/ScottishParliamentFront.JPG/220px-ScottishParliamentFront.JPG" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/ScottishParliamentFront.JPG/330px-ScottishParliamentFront.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/ScottishParliamentFront.JPG/440px-ScottishParliamentFront.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="2144" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ScottishParliamentFront.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The public entrance of the Scottish Parliament building, opened in October 2004.</div></div></div>
<p>Since September 2004, the official home of the Scottish Parliament has been a new <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament_Building" title="Scottish Parliament Building">Scottish Parliament Building</a>, in the Holyrood area of Edinburgh. The Scottish Parliament building was designed by Spanish architect <a href="/wiki/Enric_Miralles" title="Enric Miralles">Enric Miralles</a> in partnership with local Edinburgh Architecture firm <a href="/wiki/RMJM" title="RMJM">RMJM</a> which was led by Design Principal <a href="/wiki/Tony_Kettle" title="Tony Kettle">Tony Kettle</a>. Some of the principal features of the complex include leaf-shaped buildings, a grass-roofed branch merging into adjacent parkland and <a href="/wiki/Gabion" title="Gabion">gabion</a> walls formed from the stones of previous buildings. Throughout the building there are many repeated motifs, such as shapes based on <a href="/wiki/Henry_Raeburn" title="Henry Raeburn">Raeburn's</a> <a href="/wiki/The_Skating_Minister" title="The Skating Minister">Skating Minister</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Crow-stepped_gable" title="Crow-stepped gable">Crow-stepped gables</a> and the upturned boat skylights of the Garden Lobby, complete the unique<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> architecture. <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Elizabeth II of the United Kingdom">Queen Elizabeth II</a> opened the new building on 9 October 2004.
</p><p>In March 2006, one of the Holyrood building's roof beams slipped out of its support and was left dangling above the back benches during a debate.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The debating chamber was subsequently closed, and MSPs moved to <a href="/wiki/The_Hub_(Edinburgh)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Hub (Edinburgh)">The Hub</a> for one week, whilst inspections were carried out.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> During repairs, all chamber business was conducted in the Parliament's committee room two.
</p>
<h3><span id="Temporary_accommodation_1999.E2.80.932004"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Temporary_accommodation_1999–2004">Temporary accommodation 1999–2004</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Temporary accommodation 1999–2004">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>While the permanent building at Holyrood was being constructed, a temporary home for the Parliament was found in Edinburgh.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/General_Assembly_Hall_of_the_Church_of_Scotland" title="General Assembly Hall of the Church of Scotland">General Assembly Hall</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Scotland" title="Church of Scotland">Church of Scotland</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Mile" title="Royal Mile">Royal Mile</a> was chosen to host the Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Official photographs and television interviews were held in the courtyard adjoining the Assembly Hall, which is part of the <a href="/wiki/New_College,_Edinburgh" title="New College, Edinburgh">School of Divinity</a> of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Edinburgh" title="University of Edinburgh">University of Edinburgh</a>. This building was vacated twice to allow for the meeting of the <a href="/wiki/General_Assembly_of_the_Church_of_Scotland" title="General Assembly of the Church of Scotland">Church's General Assembly</a>. In May 2000, the Parliament was temporarily relocated to the former <a href="/wiki/Strathclyde_Regional_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Strathclyde Regional Council">Strathclyde Regional Council</a> debating chamber in Glasgow,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> and to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Aberdeen" title="University of Aberdeen">University of Aberdeen</a> in May 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Officials">Officials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Officials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Presiding_Officer_of_the_Scottish_Parliament" title="Presiding Officer of the Scottish Parliament">Presiding Officer of the Scottish Parliament</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Her_Majesty_Queen_Elizabeth_II_at_the_opening_of_the_Scottish_Parliament.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Her_Majesty_Queen_Elizabeth_II_at_the_opening_of_the_Scottish_Parliament.jpg/220px-Her_Majesty_Queen_Elizabeth_II_at_the_opening_of_the_Scottish_Parliament.jpg" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Her_Majesty_Queen_Elizabeth_II_at_the_opening_of_the_Scottish_Parliament.jpg/330px-Her_Majesty_Queen_Elizabeth_II_at_the_opening_of_the_Scottish_Parliament.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Her_Majesty_Queen_Elizabeth_II_at_the_opening_of_the_Scottish_Parliament.jpg/440px-Her_Majesty_Queen_Elizabeth_II_at_the_opening_of_the_Scottish_Parliament.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3508" data-file-height="2480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Her_Majesty_Queen_Elizabeth_II_at_the_opening_of_the_Scottish_Parliament.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> at the opening of the Scottish Parliament on 1 July 1999 alongside then <a href="/wiki/First_Minister_of_Scotland" title="First Minister of Scotland">First Minister of Scotland</a> <a href="/wiki/Donald_Dewar" title="Donald Dewar">Donald Dewar</a> and then Presiding Officer <a href="/wiki/David_Steel,_Baron_Steel_of_Aikwood" class="mw-redirect" title="David Steel, Baron Steel of Aikwood">Lord Steel of Aikwood</a></div></div></div>
<p>After each election to the Scottish Parliament, at the beginning of each parliamentary session, Parliament elects one MSP to serve as <a href="/wiki/Presiding_Officer_of_the_Scottish_Parliament" title="Presiding Officer of the Scottish Parliament">Presiding Officer</a>, the equivalent of the speaker in other legislatures, and two MSPs to serve as deputies. The Presiding Officer (currently <a href="/wiki/Ken_Macintosh" title="Ken Macintosh">Ken Macintosh</a>) and deputies (currently <a href="/wiki/Linda_Fabiani" title="Linda Fabiani">Linda Fabiani</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christine_Grahame" title="Christine Grahame">Christine Grahame</a>) are elected by a <a href="/wiki/Secret_ballot" title="Secret ballot">secret ballot</a> of the 129 MSPs, which is the only secret ballot conducted in the Scottish Parliament. Principally, the role of the Presiding Officer is to chair chamber proceedings and the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliamentary_Corporate_Body" title="Scottish Parliamentary Corporate Body">Scottish Parliamentary Corporate Body</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> When chairing meetings of the Parliament, the Presiding Officer and his/her deputies must be politically impartial.<sup id="cite_ref-PresidingOfficer_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PresidingOfficer-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> During debates, the Presiding Officer (or the deputy) is assisted by the parliamentary clerks, who give advice on how to interpret the <a href="/wiki/Rules_of_order" class="mw-redirect" title="Rules of order">standing orders</a> that govern the proceedings of meetings. A vote clerk sits in front of the Presiding Officer and operates the electronic voting equipment and chamber clocks.<sup id="cite_ref-Chamber_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chamber-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As a member of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliamentary_Corporate_Body" title="Scottish Parliamentary Corporate Body">Scottish Parliamentary Corporate Body</a>, the Presiding Officer is responsible for ensuring that the Parliament functions effectively and has the staff, property and resources it requires to operate.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Convening the Parliamentary Bureau, which allocates time and sets the work agenda in the chamber, is another of the roles of the Presiding Officer. Under the Standing Orders of the Parliament the Bureau consists of the Presiding Officer and one representative from each political party with five or more seats in the Parliament. Amongst the duties of the Bureau are to agree the timetable of business in the chamber, establish the number, remit and membership of parliamentary committees and regulate the passage of legislation (bills) through the Parliament. The Presiding Officer also represents the Scottish Parliament at home and abroad in an official capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-PresidingOfficer_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PresidingOfficer-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Presiding Officer controls debates by calling on members to speak. If a member believes that a rule (or standing order) has been breached, he or she may raise a "<a href="/wiki/Point_of_order" title="Point of order">point of order</a>", on which the Presiding Officer makes a ruling that is not subject to any debate or appeal. The Presiding Officer may also discipline members who fail to observe the rules of the Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-PresidingOfficer_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PresidingOfficer-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_Secretary_for_Government_Business_and_Constitutional_Relations" title="Cabinet Secretary for Government Business and Constitutional Relations">Cabinet Secretary for Government Business and Constitutional Relations</a>, supported by the <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Parliamentary_Business" class="mw-redirect" title="Minister for Parliamentary Business">Minister for Parliamentary Business</a>, is responsible for steering the Scottish Government's executive business through Parliament.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Parliamentary_chamber">Parliamentary chamber</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Parliamentary chamber">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Debating_chamber,_Scottish_Parliament_(31-05-2006).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Debating_chamber%2C_Scottish_Parliament_%2831-05-2006%29.jpg/220px-Debating_chamber%2C_Scottish_Parliament_%2831-05-2006%29.jpg" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Debating_chamber%2C_Scottish_Parliament_%2831-05-2006%29.jpg/330px-Debating_chamber%2C_Scottish_Parliament_%2831-05-2006%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Debating_chamber%2C_Scottish_Parliament_%2831-05-2006%29.jpg/440px-Debating_chamber%2C_Scottish_Parliament_%2831-05-2006%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1587" data-file-height="1161" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Debating_chamber,_Scottish_Parliament_(31-05-2006).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Seating in the <a href="/wiki/Debating_chamber" class="mw-redirect" title="Debating chamber">debating chamber</a> is arranged in a semicircle, with ministers sitting in the front section of the semicircle, directly opposite the presiding officer and parliamentary clerks.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Debating_chamber" class="mw-redirect" title="Debating chamber">debating chamber</a> of the Scottish Parliament has seating arranged in a <a href="/wiki/Hemicycle_(chamber)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hemicycle (chamber)">hemicycle</a>, a design which is common across European legislatures, intended to encourage consensus and compromise.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> There are 131 seats in the debating chamber. Of the total 131 seats, 129 are occupied by the Parliament's elected MSPs and two are seats for the Scottish Law Officers—the <a href="/wiki/Lord_Advocate" title="Lord Advocate">Lord Advocate</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Solicitor_General_for_Scotland" title="Solicitor General for Scotland">Solicitor General for Scotland</a>, who are not elected members of the Parliament but are members of the Scottish Government. As such, the Law Officers may attend and speak in the plenary meetings of the Parliament but, as they are not elected MSPs, cannot vote.
</p><p>Members are able to sit anywhere in the debating chamber, but typically sit in their party groupings.<sup id="cite_ref-Chamber_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chamber-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The First Minister, Scottish <a href="/wiki/List_of_Scottish_Governments" title="List of Scottish Governments">cabinet ministers</a> and Law officers sit in the front row, in the middle section of the chamber. The largest party in the Parliament sits in the middle of the semicircle, with opposing parties on either side.<sup id="cite_ref-Chamber_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chamber-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The Presiding Officer, parliamentary clerks and officials sit opposite members at the front of the debating chamber.
</p><p>In front of the Presiding Officers' desk is the parliamentary <a href="/wiki/Ceremonial_mace" title="Ceremonial mace">mace</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_mace_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_mace-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> which is made from silver and <a href="/wiki/Inlay" title="Inlay">inlaid</a> with gold panned from Scottish rivers and inscribed with the words: <i>Wisdom</i>, <i>Compassion</i>, <i>Justice</i> and <i>Integrity</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-mace_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mace-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The words <i>There shall be a Scottish Parliament</i>, which are the first words of the Scotland Act, are inscribed around the head of the mace,<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_mace_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_mace-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mace_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mace-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> which has a ceremonial role in the meetings of Parliament, representing the authority of the Parliament to make laws.<sup id="cite_ref-mace_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mace-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Presented to the Scottish Parliament by the Queen upon Parliament's official opening in July 1999, the mace is displayed in a glass case, suspended from the lid. At the beginning of each sitting in the chamber, the lid of the case is rotated so that the mace is above the glass, to symbolise that a full meeting of the Parliament is taking place.<sup id="cite_ref-Chamber_29-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chamber-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Proceedings">Proceedings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Proceedings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Queen_at_the_Scottish_Parliament.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/The_Queen_at_the_Scottish_Parliament.jpg/220px-The_Queen_at_the_Scottish_Parliament.jpg" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/The_Queen_at_the_Scottish_Parliament.jpg/330px-The_Queen_at_the_Scottish_Parliament.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/The_Queen_at_the_Scottish_Parliament.jpg/440px-The_Queen_at_the_Scottish_Parliament.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3508" data-file-height="2480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Queen_at_the_Scottish_Parliament.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Scotland" title="Crown of Scotland">Crown of Scotland</a> is carried by <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Douglas-Hamilton,_16th_Duke_of_Hamilton" title="Alexander Douglas-Hamilton, 16th Duke of Hamilton">The 16th Duke of Hamilton</a> as <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> leaves the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament_Building#Debating_chamber" title="Scottish Parliament Building">Chamber</a>, following the Opening of the <a href="/wiki/4th_Scottish_Parliament" title="4th Scottish Parliament">fourth Session</a> in July 2011.</div></div></div>
<p>Parliament typically sits Tuesdays, Wednesdays and Thursdays from early January to late June and from early September to mid December, with two-week recesses in April and October.<sup id="cite_ref-Brief_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brief-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Plenary meetings in the debating chamber usually take place on Wednesday afternoons from 2&#160;pm to 6&#160;pm and on Thursdays from 9:15&#160;am to 6&#160;pm.<sup id="cite_ref-Brief_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brief-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Chamber debates and committee meetings are open to the public. Entry is free, but booking in advance is recommended due to limited space. Parliament TV is a webcast and archive of Parliamentary business back to 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> and on the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>'s parliamentary channel <a href="/wiki/BBC_Parliament" title="BBC Parliament">BBC Parliament</a>. Proceedings are also recorded in text form, in print and online, in the <i>Official Report</i>, which is the substantially verbatim transcript of parliamentary debates.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since September 2012, the first item of business on Tuesday afternoons is usually Time for Reflection<sup id="cite_ref-Reflection_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reflection-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> at which a speaker addresses members for up to four minutes, sharing a perspective on issues of <a href="/wiki/Faith" title="Faith">faith</a>. This contrasts with the formal style of "Prayers", which is the first item of business in meetings of the <a href="/wiki/British_House_of_Commons" class="mw-redirect" title="British House of Commons">House of Commons</a>. Speakers are drawn from across Scotland and are chosen to represent the balance of religious beliefs according to the <a href="/wiki/Census_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Census in the United Kingdom">Scottish census</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Reflection_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reflection-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Invitations to address Parliament in this manner are determined by the Presiding Officer on the advice of the parliamentary bureau. Faith groups can make direct representations to the Presiding Officer to nominate speakers. Before September 2012, Time for reflection was held on Wednesday afternoons.<sup id="cite_ref-Reflection_39-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reflection-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Presiding Officer (or Deputy Presiding Officer) decides who speaks in chamber debates and the amount of time for which they are allowed to speak.<sup id="cite_ref-PresidingOfficer_28-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PresidingOfficer-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Normally, the Presiding Officer tries to achieve a balance between different viewpoints and political parties when selecting members to speak.<sup id="cite_ref-Chamber_29-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chamber-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Typically, ministers or party leaders open debates, with opening speakers given between 5 and 20 minutes, and succeeding speakers allocated less time.<sup id="cite_ref-Chamber_29-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chamber-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The Presiding Officer can reduce speaking time if a large number of members wish to participate in the debate. Debate is more informal than in some parliamentary systems.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Members may call each other directly by name, rather than by constituency or cabinet position, and hand clapping is allowed.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Speeches to the chamber are normally delivered in English, but members may use <a href="/wiki/Scots_language" title="Scots language">Scots</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Gaelic</a>, or any other language with the agreement of the Presiding Officer.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The Scottish Parliament has conducted debates in the Gaelic language.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Each sitting day, normally at 5&#160;pm, MSPs decide on all the <a href="/wiki/Motion_(democracy)" title="Motion (democracy)">motions</a> and amendments that have been moved that day. This "Decision Time" is heralded by the sounding of the division bell, which is heard throughout the Parliamentary campus and alerts MSPs who are not in the chamber to return and vote.<sup id="cite_ref-Chamber_29-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chamber-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> At Decision Time, the Presiding Officer puts questions on the motions and amendments by reading out the name of the motion or amendment as well as the proposer and asking "<i>Are we all agreed?</i>", to which the chamber first votes orally. If there is audible dissent, the Presiding Officer announces "<i>There will be a division</i>" and members vote by means of electronic consoles on their desks. Each MSP has a unique access card with a <a href="/wiki/Integrated_circuit" title="Integrated circuit">microchip</a> which, when inserted into the console, identifies them and allows them to vote.<sup id="cite_ref-Chamber_29-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chamber-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> As a result, the outcome of each division is known in seconds.
</p><p>The outcome of most votes can be predicted beforehand since political parties normally instruct members which way to vote. Parties entrust some MSPs, known as <a href="/wiki/Whip_(politics)" title="Whip (politics)">whips</a>, with the task of ensuring that party members vote according to the party line.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> MSPs do not tend to vote against such instructions, since those who do are unlikely to reach higher political ranks in their parties.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Errant members can be deselected as official party candidates during future elections, and, in serious cases, may be expelled from their parties outright.<sup id="cite_ref-Kingdom2_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kingdom2-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Thus, as with many Parliaments, the independence of Members of the Scottish Parliament tends to be low, and backbench rebellions by members who are discontent with their party's policies are rare.<sup id="cite_ref-Kingdom2_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kingdom2-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> In some circumstances, however, parties announce "free votes", which allows Members to vote as they please. This is typically done on <a href="/wiki/Morality" title="Morality">moral</a> issues.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Immediately after Decision Time a "Members Debate" is held, which lasts for 45 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-Chamber_29-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chamber-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Members Business is a debate on a motion proposed by an MSP who is not a <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Executive" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Executive">Scottish minister</a>. Such motions are on issues which may be of interest to a particular area such as a member's own constituency, an upcoming or past event or any other item which would otherwise not be accorded official parliamentary time. As well as the proposer, other members normally contribute to the debate. The relevant minister, whose department the debate and motion relate to "winds up" the debate by speaking after all other participants.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Committees">Committees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Committees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Committees_of_the_Scottish_Parliament" title="Committees of the Scottish Parliament">Committees of the Scottish Parliament</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Entrance_Plazza,_National_Galleries_of_Scotland.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Entrance_Plazza%2C_National_Galleries_of_Scotland.jpg/220px-Entrance_Plazza%2C_National_Galleries_of_Scotland.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Entrance_Plazza%2C_National_Galleries_of_Scotland.jpg/330px-Entrance_Plazza%2C_National_Galleries_of_Scotland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Entrance_Plazza%2C_National_Galleries_of_Scotland.jpg/440px-Entrance_Plazza%2C_National_Galleries_of_Scotland.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Entrance_Plazza,_National_Galleries_of_Scotland.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Private Bill Committees are set up to deal with the legislation required for major <a href="/wiki/Public_sector" title="Public sector">public sector</a> infrastructure projects, such as the underground extensions to the <a href="/wiki/National_Gallery_of_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="National Gallery of Scotland">National Gallery of Scotland</a> in 2003.</div></div></div>
<p>Much of the work of the Scottish Parliament is done in <a href="/wiki/Committee" title="Committee">committee</a>. The role of committees is stronger in the Scottish Parliament than in other parliamentary systems, partly as a means of strengthening the role of backbenchers in their scrutiny of the government<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> and partly to compensate for the fact that there is no revising chamber. The principal role of committees in the Scottish Parliament is to take evidence from witnesses, conduct inquiries and scrutinise legislation.<sup id="cite_ref-Committee_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Committee-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Committee meetings take place on Tuesday, Wednesday and Thursday morning when Parliament is sitting. Committees can also meet at other locations throughout Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Committees comprise a small number of MSPs, with membership reflecting the balance of parties across Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-Committee_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Committee-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> There are different committees with their functions set out in different ways. Mandatory Committees are committees which are set down under the Scottish Parliament's standing orders, which govern their remits and proceedings.<sup id="cite_ref-CommitteeInfo_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CommitteeInfo-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The current Mandatory Committees in the fourth Session of the Scottish Parliament are: Public <a href="/wiki/Audit" title="Audit">Audit</a>; Equal Opportunities; <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Europe" title="Politics of Europe">European</a> and External Relations; Finance; Public Petitions; Standards, Procedures and Public Appointments; and Delegated Powers and Law Reform.<sup id="cite_ref-Committee_49-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Committee-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Subject Committees are established at the beginning of each parliamentary session, and again the members on each committee reflect the balance of parties across Parliament. Typically each committee corresponds with one (or more) of the departments (or ministries) of the Scottish Government. The current Subject Committees in the fourth Session are: Economy, Energy and Tourism; <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Scotland" title="Education in Scotland">Education and Culture</a>; <a href="/wiki/NHS_Scotland" title="NHS Scotland">Health and Sport</a>; <a href="/wiki/Scots_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="Scots Law">Justice</a>; <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_Scotland" title="Local government in Scotland">Local Government and Regeneration</a>; Rural Affairs, Climate Change and Environment; Welfare Reform; and <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Scotland" title="Transport in Scotland">Infrastructure and Capital Investment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Committee_49-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Committee-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A further type of committee is normally set up to scrutinise <a href="/wiki/Private_bill" title="Private bill">private bills</a> submitted to the Scottish Parliament by an outside party or promoter who is not a member of the Scottish Parliament or Scottish Government. Private bills normally relate to large-scale development projects such as infrastructure projects that require the use of land or property.<sup id="cite_ref-PrivateBillCommitteeMeetings_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PrivateBillCommitteeMeetings-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Private Bill Committees have been set up to consider legislation on issues such as the development of the <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Tram_Network" class="mw-redirect" title="Edinburgh Tram Network">Edinburgh Tram Network</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Airport_Rail_Link" title="Glasgow Airport Rail Link">Glasgow Airport Rail Link</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Airdrie-Bathgate_Rail_Link" class="mw-redirect" title="Airdrie-Bathgate Rail Link">Airdrie-Bathgate Rail Link</a> and extensions to the <a href="/wiki/National_Gallery_of_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="National Gallery of Scotland">National Gallery of Scotland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PrivateBillCommitteeMeetings_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PrivateBillCommitteeMeetings-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legislative_functions">Legislative functions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Legislative functions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Constitution_and_powers">Constitution and powers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Constitution and powers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Scotland_Act_1998" title="Scotland Act 1998">Scotland Act 1998</a>, which was passed by the Parliament of the United Kingdom and given <a href="/wiki/Royal_assent" title="Royal assent">royal assent</a> by Queen Elizabeth II on 19 November 1998,<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> governs the functions and role of the Scottish Parliament and delimits its legislative competence.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Scotland_Act_2012" title="Scotland Act 2012">Scotland Act 2012</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Scotland_Act_2016" title="Scotland Act 2016">Scotland Act 2016</a> extended the devolved competencies. For the purposes of <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_sovereignty" title="Parliamentary sovereignty">parliamentary sovereignty</a>, the Parliament of the United Kingdom at Westminster continues to constitute the supreme legislature of Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-UKParliament_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UKParliament-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> However, under the terms of the Scotland Acts, Westminster agreed to devolve some of its responsibilities over Scottish domestic policy to the Scottish Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-UKParliament_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UKParliament-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Such "devolved matters" include education, health, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Executive_Environment_and_Rural_Affairs_Department" title="Scottish Executive Environment and Rural Affairs Department">agriculture</a> and justice.<sup id="cite_ref-devolvedmatters_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-devolvedmatters-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The Scotland Act 1998 enabled the Scottish Parliament to pass <a href="/wiki/Primary_legislation" class="mw-redirect" title="Primary legislation">primary legislation</a> on these issues. A degree of domestic authority, and all <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Foreign relations of the United Kingdom">foreign policy</a>, remain with the UK Parliament in Westminster.<sup id="cite_ref-devolvedmatters_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-devolvedmatters-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The Scottish Parliament has the power to pass laws and has tax powers.<sup id="cite_ref-powers_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-powers-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Another of the roles of the Parliament is to hold the Scottish Government to account.<sup id="cite_ref-Cairney_2014_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cairney_2014-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The specific devolved matters are all subjects which are not explicitly stated in Schedule 5 to the Scotland Act as <a href="/wiki/Reserved_matters" class="mw-redirect" title="Reserved matters">reserved matters</a>. All matters that are not specifically reserved are automatically devolved to the Scottish Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-devolvedmatters_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-devolvedmatters-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Most importantly, this includes agriculture, fisheries and forestry, <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Scotland" title="Economy of Scotland">economic development</a>, education, environment, food standards, consumer advocacy, health, abortion, home affairs, Scots law, <a href="/wiki/Courts_in_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Courts in Scotland">courts</a>, legal profession, police and fire services, prisons, control of air guns, local government, <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Scotland" title="Sport in Scotland">sport</a> and the arts, transport, road signs, speed limits, rail franchising, training, <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Scotland" title="Tourism in Scotland">tourism</a>, research and statistics, social work and various welfare and housing related benefits.<sup id="cite_ref-devolvedmatters_56-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-devolvedmatters-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> In terms of tax powers, the Scottish Parliament has full control over income tax rates and thresholds on all non-savings and non-dividend income liable for tax by taxpayers resident in Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The Scottish Parliament also has full control over <a href="/wiki/Land_and_Buildings_Transaction_Tax" title="Land and Buildings Transaction Tax">Land and Buildings Transaction Tax</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Landfill_Tax" title="Scottish Landfill Tax">Scottish Landfill Tax</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Reserved matters are subjects that are outside the legislative competence of the Scotland Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-powers_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-powers-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The Scottish Parliament is unable to legislate on such issues that are reserved to, and dealt with at, Westminster (and where Ministerial functions usually lie with UK Government ministers). These include <a href="/wiki/Media_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Media of the United Kingdom">broadcasting</a> policy, <a href="/wiki/Her_Majesty%27s_Civil_Service" class="mw-redirect" title="Her Majesty&#39;s Civil Service">civil service</a>, common markets for UK goods and services, <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Constitution of the United Kingdom">constitution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Energy_use_and_conservation_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Energy use and conservation in the United Kingdom">electricity</a>, coal, oil, gas, <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Nuclear power in the United Kingdom">nuclear energy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(United_Kingdom)" title="Ministry of Defence (United Kingdom)">defence</a> and national security, <a href="/wiki/Misuse_of_Drugs_Act_1971" title="Misuse of Drugs Act 1971">drug policy</a>, employment, foreign policy and relations with Europe, most aspects of <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Transport in the United Kingdom">transport</a> safety and regulation, <a href="/wiki/National_Lottery_(United_Kingdom)" title="National Lottery (United Kingdom)">National Lottery</a>, protection of borders, most aspects of <a href="/wiki/National_Insurance" title="National Insurance">social security</a> and stability of UK's fiscal, <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Economy of the United Kingdom">economic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Banknotes_of_the_pound_sterling" title="Banknotes of the pound sterling">monetary</a> system.<sup id="cite_ref-devolvedmatters_56-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-devolvedmatters-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Members of the public take part in Parliament in two ways that are not the case at Westminster: a public <a href="/wiki/Petition" title="Petition">petitioning</a> system, and cross-party groups on policy topics which the interested public join and attend meetings of, alongside MSPs.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The Parliament is able to debate any issue (including those reserved to Westminster) but is unable to make laws on issues that are outside its legislative competence.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bills">Bills</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Bills">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Act_of_the_Scottish_Parliament" title="Act of the Scottish Parliament">Act of the Scottish Parliament</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Scottish_Parliament_Act.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Scottish_Parliament_Act.JPG/220px-Scottish_Parliament_Act.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Scottish_Parliament_Act.JPG/330px-Scottish_Parliament_Act.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Scottish_Parliament_Act.JPG/440px-Scottish_Parliament_Act.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Scottish_Parliament_Act.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>After a <a href="/wiki/Bill_(proposed_law)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bill (proposed law)">bill</a> has passed through all legislative stages, it becomes an <a href="/wiki/Act_of_the_Scottish_Parliament" title="Act of the Scottish Parliament">Act of the Scottish Parliament</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>As the Scottish Parliament is able to make laws on the areas constitutionally devolved to it, the legislative process begins with <a href="/wiki/Bill_(proposed_law)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bill (proposed law)">bills</a> (draft laws) which are presented to Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-Bills_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bills-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bills can be introduced to Parliament in a number of ways; the Scottish Government can introduce new laws or amendments to existing laws as a bill; a committee of the Parliament can present a bill in one of the areas under its remit; a member of the Scottish Parliament can introduce a bill as a private member; or a <a href="/wiki/Private_bill" title="Private bill">private bill</a> can be submitted to Parliament by an outside proposer.<sup id="cite_ref-Bills_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bills-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Most draft laws are government bills introduced by ministers in the governing party (or parties). Bills pass through Parliament in a number of stages before receiving royal assent, whereupon they become <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_the_Scottish_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Acts of the Scottish Parliament">Acts of the Scottish Parliament</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Scrutiny_of_government">Scrutiny of government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Scrutiny of government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Declaration_Glasgow_Kelvin.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Declaration_Glasgow_Kelvin.JPG/220px-Declaration_Glasgow_Kelvin.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Declaration_Glasgow_Kelvin.JPG/330px-Declaration_Glasgow_Kelvin.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Declaration_Glasgow_Kelvin.JPG/440px-Declaration_Glasgow_Kelvin.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1632" data-file-height="1224" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Declaration_Glasgow_Kelvin.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The result for the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Kelvin_(Scottish_Parliament_constituency)" title="Glasgow Kelvin (Scottish Parliament constituency)">Kelvin constituency</a> being declared at the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament_election,_2007" title="Scottish Parliament election, 2007">Scottish Parliament election, 2007</a>. Ordinary general elections for the Scottish Parliament are held on the first Thursday in May every four years.</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Government" title="Scottish Government">Scottish Government</a></div>
<p>The party, or parties, that hold the majority of seats in the Parliament forms the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Government" title="Scottish Government">Scottish Government</a>. In contrast to many other parliamentary systems, Parliament elects a <a href="/wiki/First_Minister_of_Scotland" title="First Minister of Scotland">First Minister</a> from a number of candidates at the beginning of each parliamentary term (after a <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Scotland" title="Elections in Scotland">general election</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-FM_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FM-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Any member can put their name forward to be First Minister, and a vote is taken by all members of Parliament. Normally, the leader of the largest party is returned as First Minister, and head of the Scottish Government.<sup id="cite_ref-FM_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FM-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Theoretically, Parliament also elects the Scottish Ministers who form the government of Scotland and sit in the Scottish cabinet, but such ministers are, in practice, appointed to their roles by the First Minister.<sup id="cite_ref-Nominations_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nominations-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Junior ministers, who do not attend cabinet, are also appointed to assist Scottish ministers in their departments. Most ministers and their juniors are drawn from amongst the elected MSPs, with the exception of Scotland's Chief Law Officers: the Lord Advocate and the Solicitor General.<sup id="cite_ref-Brief_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brief-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Whilst the First Minister chooses the ministers – and may decide to remove them at any time – the formal appointment or dismissal is made by the Sovereign.<sup id="cite_ref-Nominations_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nominations-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Under the Scotland Act 1998, ordinary general elections for the Scottish Parliament are held on the first Thursday in May every four years (<a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament_election,_1999" title="Scottish Parliament election, 1999">1999</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament_election,_2003" title="Scottish Parliament election, 2003">2003</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament_election,_2007" title="Scottish Parliament election, 2007">2007</a> and so on).<sup id="cite_ref-ScotlandAct2_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ScotlandAct2-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The date of the poll may be varied by up to one month either way by the Monarch on the proposal of the Presiding Officer.<sup id="cite_ref-ScotlandAct2_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ScotlandAct2-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> If the Parliament itself resolves that it should be dissolved (with at least two-thirds of the Members voting in favour), or if the Parliament fails to nominate one of its members to be First Minister within 28 days of a General Election or of the position becoming vacant,<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> the Presiding Officer proposes a date for an extraordinary general election and the Parliament is dissolved by the Queen by <a href="/wiki/Royal_proclamation" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal proclamation">royal proclamation</a>. Extraordinary general elections are in addition to ordinary general elections, unless held less than six months before the due date of an ordinary general election, in which case they supplant it. The following ordinary election reverts to the first Thursday in May, a multiple of four years after 1999 (i.e., 5 May 2011, 7 May 2015, etc.).<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Several procedures enable the Scottish Parliament to scrutinise the Government.<sup id="cite_ref-Cairney_2014_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cairney_2014-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The First Minister or members of the cabinet can deliver statements to Parliament upon which MSPs are invited to question. For example, at the beginning of each parliamentary year, the First Minister delivers a statement to the chamber setting out the Government's legislative programme for the forthcoming year.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> After the statement has been delivered, the leaders of the opposition parties and other MSPs question the First Minister on issues related to the substance of the statement.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Parliamentary time is also set aside for question periods in the debating chamber. A "General Question Time" takes place on a Thursday between 11:40&#160;a.m. and noon where members can direct questions to any member of the Scottish Government.<sup id="cite_ref-Brief_36-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brief-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> At 2:30&#160;pm, a 40-minute-long themed "Question Time" takes place, where members can ask questions of ministers in departments that are selected for questioning that sitting day, such as health and justice or education and transport.<sup id="cite_ref-Brief_36-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brief-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Between noon and 12:30&#160;p.m. on Thursdays, when Parliament is sitting, <a href="/wiki/First_Minister%27s_Question_Time_(Scotland)" class="mw-redirect" title="First Minister&#39;s Question Time (Scotland)">First Minister's Question Time</a> takes place.<sup id="cite_ref-Brief_36-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brief-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> This gives members an opportunity to question the First Minister directly on issues under their jurisdiction.
</p><p>Members who wish to ask general or themed questions, or questions of the First Minister, must lodge them with parliamentary clerks beforehand and selections are made by the Presiding Officer. Written questions may also be submitted by members to ministers. Written questions and answers are published in the <i>Official Report</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Brief_36-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brief-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Members.2C_constituencies_and_voting_systems"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Members,_constituencies_and_voting_systems">Members, constituencies and voting systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Members, constituencies and voting systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MSP_Group_Shot_Dec2004-lg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/98/MSP_Group_Shot_Dec2004-lg.jpg/220px-MSP_Group_Shot_Dec2004-lg.jpg" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/98/MSP_Group_Shot_Dec2004-lg.jpg/330px-MSP_Group_Shot_Dec2004-lg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/9/98/MSP_Group_Shot_Dec2004-lg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="397" data-file-height="251" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MSP_Group_Shot_Dec2004-lg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 2003 election's 129 Members of the Scottish Parliament; 73 represented individual constituencies and 56 represented eight additional member regions</div></div></div>
<p>Elections for the Scottish Parliament were amongst the first in Britain to use a <a href="/wiki/Mixed_member_proportional_representation" class="mw-redirect" title="Mixed member proportional representation">mixed member proportional representation</a> (MMP) system.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The system is a form of the <a href="/wiki/Additional_Member_System" title="Additional Member System">additional member</a> method (AMS) of <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a>, and is better known as such in Britain. Under the system, voters are given two votes: one for a specific candidate and one for a political party.
</p><p>Of the 129 MSPs, 73 are elected to represent <a href="/wiki/Plurality_voting_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Plurality voting system">first past the post</a> <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament_constituencies_and_regions" title="Scottish Parliament constituencies and regions">constituencies</a> and are known as "Constituency MSPs".<sup id="cite_ref-ScotParlWorks_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ScotParlWorks-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Voters choose one member to represent the constituency, and the member with most votes is returned as a constituency MSP. The 73 Scottish Parliament constituencies shared the same boundaries as the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_constituencies" title="United Kingdom constituencies">UK Parliament constituencies</a> in Scotland, prior to the 2005 reduction in the number of Scottish  MPs, with the exception of <a href="/wiki/Orkney" title="Orkney">Orkney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shetland" title="Shetland">Shetland</a> which each return their own constituency MSP. Currently, the average Scottish Parliament constituency comprises 55,000 electors.<sup id="cite_ref-Constituency_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constituency-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Given the geographical distribution of <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Demographics of Scotland">population in Scotland</a>, this results in constituencies of a smaller area in the <a href="/wiki/Central_Lowlands" title="Central Lowlands">Central Lowlands</a>, where the bulk of Scotland's population live, and much larger constituency areas in the north and west of the country, which have a low population density. The island archipelagos of Orkney, Shetland and the <a href="/wiki/Western_Isles_(Scottish_Parliament_constituency)" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Isles (Scottish Parliament constituency)">Western Isles</a> comprise a much smaller number of electors, due to their dispersed population.<sup id="cite_ref-Constituency_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constituency-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> If a Constituency MSP resigns from Parliament, this triggers a by-election in his or her constituency, where a replacement MSP is returned from one of the parties by the plurality system.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The remaining 56 MSPs, called "List MSPs", are elected by an additional members system, which seeks to make the overall results more proportional, countering any distortions in the constituency results. Seven List MSPs are elected from each of eight <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament_constituencies_and_regions#Regions" title="Scottish Parliament constituencies and regions">electoral regions</a>, of which constituencies are sub-divisions:<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Central_Scotland_(Scottish_Parliament_electoral_region)" title="Central Scotland (Scottish Parliament electoral region)">Central Scotland</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Glasgow_(Scottish_Parliament_electoral_region)" title="Glasgow (Scottish Parliament electoral region)">Glasgow</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Highlands_and_Islands_(Scottish_Parliament_electoral_region)" title="Highlands and Islands (Scottish Parliament electoral region)">Highlands and Islands</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lothian_(Scottish_Parliament_electoral_region)" title="Lothian (Scottish Parliament electoral region)">Lothian</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mid_Scotland_and_Fife_(Scottish_Parliament_electoral_region)" title="Mid Scotland and Fife (Scottish Parliament electoral region)">Mid Scotland and Fife</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/North_East_Scotland_(Scottish_Parliament_electoral_region)" title="North East Scotland (Scottish Parliament electoral region)">North East Scotland</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/South_Scotland_(Scottish_Parliament_electoral_region)" title="South Scotland (Scottish Parliament electoral region)">South Scotland</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/West_Scotland_(Scottish_Parliament_electoral_region)" title="West Scotland (Scottish Parliament electoral region)">West Scotland</a></li></ul>
<p>Each political party draws up a list of candidates standing in each electoral region, from which the List MSPs are elected.<sup id="cite_ref-AMSSystem_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AMSSystem-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> When a List MSP resigns, the next person on the resigning MSPs' party's list takes the seat.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The total number of seats in the Parliament are allocated to parties proportionally to the number of votes received in the second vote of the ballot using the <a href="/wiki/D%27Hondt_method" title="D&#39;Hondt method">d'Hondt method</a>. For example, to determine who is awarded the first list seat, the number of list votes cast for each party is divided by one plus the number of seats the party won in the region (at this point just constituency seats). The party with the highest quotient is awarded the seat, which is then added to its constituency seats in allocating the second seat. This is repeated <a href="/wiki/Iterated_function" title="Iterated function">iteratively</a> until all available list seats are allocated.<sup id="cite_ref-AMSSystem_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AMSSystem-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The system was designed to make it all but impossible for one party to win an outright majority of seats. Nonetheless, the 2011 election saw the SNP become the first–and to date, only–party to win a majority government.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As in the House of Commons, a number of qualifications apply to being an MSP. Such qualifications were introduced under the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_Disqualification_Act_1975" title="House of Commons Disqualification Act 1975">House of Commons Disqualification Act 1975</a> and the <a href="/wiki/British_Nationality_Act_1981" title="British Nationality Act 1981">British Nationality Act 1981</a>. Specifically, members must be over the age of 18<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> and must be a <a href="/wiki/British_nationality_law" title="British nationality law">citizen of the United Kingdom</a>, the Republic of Ireland, one of the countries in the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, a citizen of a <a href="/wiki/British_overseas_territory" class="mw-redirect" title="British overseas territory">British overseas territory</a>, or a <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> citizen resident in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-Disqualifications_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Disqualifications-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Members of the police and the armed forces are disqualified from sitting in the Scottish Parliament as elected MSPs, and similarly, civil servants and members of foreign legislatures are disqualified.<sup id="cite_ref-Disqualifications_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Disqualifications-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> An individual may not sit in the Scottish Parliament if he or she is judged to be insane under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Mental_Health_(Care_and_Treatment)_(Scotland)_Act_2003" title="Mental Health (Care and Treatment) (Scotland) Act 2003">Mental Health (Care and Treatment) (Scotland) Act 2003</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Disqualifications_78-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Disqualifications-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Elections">Elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
